# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` — use `repo:^github.com/prometheus/prometheus$` filter
- `github.com/sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common` — use `repo:^github.com/sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common$` filter
- `github.com/prometheus/alertmanager` — use `repo:^github.com/prometheus/alertmanager$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/prometheus/prometheus`, `github.com/sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common`, `github.com/prometheus/alertmanager`, `github.com/sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec`

# Prometheus PromQL Query Parsing and Validation Pipeline

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that implement the PromQL query parsing and validation pipeline. Identify: the Parser interface and parser struct with ParseExpr and checkAST (in promql/parser/), the Lexer tokenizer, the AST node type definitions (Expr, VectorSelector, BinaryExpr, etc.), the generated yacc parser, the Function registry defining valid PromQL functions, the value type system used for expression type validation, and the Engine that integrates the parser.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: prometheus/prometheus.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `prometheus/prometheus` (prometheus/prometheus)
- `sourcegraph-testing/prometheus-common` (prometheus/client_golang)
- `prometheus/alertmanager` (prometheus/alertmanager)
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a comprehensive analysis of the PromQL parsing pipeline, including:

### **Core Components Found:**

1. **Parser Interface** (`promql/parser/parse.go`): The `Parser` interface with `ParseExpr()` and `checkAST()` methods
2. **AST Definitions** (`promql/parser/ast.go`): Complete node hierarchy including `Expr`, `VectorSelector`, `BinaryExpr`, `MatrixSelector`, `AggregateExpr`, `Call`, and 8+ other expression types
3. **Lexer** (`promql/parser/lex.go`): Tokenization with `Item` and `ItemType` definitions
4. **Function Registry** (`promql/parser/functions.go`): 100+ built-in functions defined in the `Functions` map
5. **Value Type System** (`promql/parser/value.go`): `ValueType` constants and `Value` interface for type validation
6. **YACC Parser** (`promql/parser/generated_parser.y` and `generated_parser.y.go`): Generated parser handling syntax and precedence
7. **Engine Integration** (`promql/engine.go`): Main `Engine` struct integrating the parser into query execution
8. **Function Implementations** (`promql/functions.go`): Actual implementations of PromQL functions
9. **Supporting Files**: Feature registry, AST utilities (printer/prettier), position tracking

The answer document provides a detailed narrative explaining how all components work together in the complete pipeline from query string input to execution output.

The `promQLParser` struct implements this interface with two key methods:\\n- `ParseExpr(input string)` - Entry point that parses a PromQL expression string\\n- `parseExpr()` - Internal recursive parser that builds the AST\\n- `checkAST(node Node)` - Validates the AST including type checking after parsing\\nThe parser uses a sync.Pool for efficient resource management and supports configuration options like experimental functions and extended range selectors.\\n\\n### 2. Lexer/Tokenizer (promql/parser/lex.go)\\nThe lexer tokenizes the input query string:\\n- `Item` struct represents a token with type, position, and value\\n- `ItemType` enumeration defines all token types (operators, aggregators, keywords, literals)\\n- The lexer uses a state machine to recognize keywords, identifiers, numbers, durations, strings, and special symbols\\n- Position tracking is maintained for error reporting via the posrange package\\n\\n### 3. AST Node Definitions (promql/parser/ast.go)\\nDefines the complete Abstract Syntax Tree node hierarchy:\\n- `Node` interface - Base interface for all AST nodes\\n- `Expr` interface - Base interface for all expression types with a `Type()` method\\n- Expression types include:\\n  - `VectorSelector` - Metric name and label matchers (e.g., `up{job=\\\"prometheus\\\"}`)\\n  - `MatrixSelector` - Range vector with time duration (e.g., `http_requests_total[5m]`)\\n  - `BinaryExpr` - Binary operations with left/right operands and optional vector matching\\n  - `AggregateExpr` - Aggregation functions (sum, avg, count, etc.) with grouping\\n  - `Call` - Function calls to built-in functions\\n  - `UnaryExpr` - Unary operations (negation)\\n  - `NumberLiteral` - Scalar numbers\\n  - `StringLiteral` - String values\\n  - `ParenExpr` - Parenthesized expressions\\n  - `SubqueryExpr` - Subqueries with time ranges\\n  - `StepInvariantExpr` - Internal optimization wrapper\\n  - `DurationExpr` - Duration literals and expressions\\n\\n### 4. Value Type System (promql/parser/value.go)\\nDefines the type system for expression validation:\\n- `ValueType` string constants: `ValueTypeVector`, `ValueTypeScalar`, `ValueTypeMatrix`, `ValueTypeString`, `ValueTypeNone`\\n- `Value` interface for runtime values with type information\\n- All Expr types implement `Type()` method returning their result type\\n\\n### 5. Function Registry (promql/parser/functions.go)\\nDefines all supported PromQL functions:\\n- `Function` struct with: Name, ArgTypes, Variadic count, ReturnType, Experimental flag\\n- `Functions` map providing a registry of 100+ built-in functions (abs, rate, increase, histogram_quantile, etc.)\\n- Functions specify their argument types for validation during type checking\\n\\n### 6. Generated Parser (promql/parser/generated_parser.y and generated_parser.y.go)\\n- `generated_parser.y` - YACC grammar file defining PromQL syntax\\n- `generated_parser.y.go` - Generated parser code produced by goyacc tool\\n- Handles operator precedence, associativity, and grammar rules\\n- Generated functions like `parseGenerated(startSymbol)` execute the YACC parser\\n\\n## Validation and Type Checking\\n\\n### 7. Feature Registry (promql/parser/features.go)\\n- `RegisterFeatures()` method registers available PromQL features\\n- Tracks enabled operators, aggregators, and functions\\n- Supports experimental features controlled by parser options\\n\\n### 8. AST Utilities (promql/parser/printer.go, prettier.go)\\n- `Tree()` function prints AST structure for debugging\\n- Pretty printing and formatting of AST back to string form\\n- Proper formatting of expressions with correct precedence\\n\\n### 9. Position Tracking (promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go)\\n- `PositionRange` struct tracks start/end positions in the input string\\n- Used for precise error reporting and highlighting\\n\\n## Query Execution Engine\\n\\n### 10. Engine Integration (promql/engine.go)\\nThe `Engine` struct integrates the parser into the query execution pipeline:\\n- Uses the Parser to parse query strings into AST\\n- Implements `NewInstantQuery()` and `NewRangeQuery()` to create executable queries\\n- Executes compiled query plans against TSDB data\\n- Handles timeout, cancellation, and resource management\\n- Contains EngineOpts for configuration including the parser instance\\n\\n### 11. Function Implementations (promql/functions.go)\\n- Defines `FunctionCall` type for function implementations\\n- Implements 100+ built-in functions matching the registry\\n- Functions operate on Vector, Matrix, Scalar values\\n- Examples: rate, increase, histogram_quantile, vector arithmetic, aggregation functions\\n\\n## Pipeline Flow\\n\\n1. **Input**: User provides PromQL query string\\n2. **Tokenization**: Lexer converts string to token stream\\n3. **Parsing**: YACC parser builds AST from tokens\\n4. **Validation**: `checkAST()` validates types and semantics\\n5. **Compilation**: Engine optimizes and prepares execution plan\\n6. **Execution**: Engine evaluates the query against time series data\\n7. **Output**: Returns query results (Vector, Matrix, Scalar, or String)\\n\\nAll files work together to provide a complete, type-safe PromQL query processing system with comprehensive error reporting and validation.\"\n}\n",

Parser Interface and Implementation (promql/parser/parse.go)\\nThe `Parser` interface defines the parsing methods. The `promQLParser` struct implements this interface with two key methods:\\n- `ParseExpr(input string)` - Entry point that parses a PromQL expression string\\n- `parseExpr()` - Internal recursive parser that builds the AST\\n- `checkAST(node Node)` - Validates the AST including type checking after parsing\\nThe parser uses a sync.Pool for efficient resource management and supports configuration options like experimental functions and extended range selectors.\\n\\n### 2. Lexer/Tokenizer (promql/parser/lex.go)\\nThe lexer tokenizes the input query string:\\n- `Item` struct represents a token with type, position, and value\\n- `ItemType` enumeration defines all token types (operators, aggregators, keywords, literals)\\n- The lexer uses a state machine to recognize keywords, identifiers, numbers, durations, strings, and special symbols\\n- Position tracking is maintained for error reporting via the posrange package\\n\\n### 3. AST Node Definitions (promql/parser/ast.go)\\nDefines the complete Abstract Syntax Tree node hierarchy:\\n- `Node` interface - Base interface for all AST nodes\\n- `Expr` interface - Base interface for all expression types with a `Type()` method\\n- Expression types include:\\n  - `VectorSelector` - Metric name and label matchers (e.g., `up{job=\\\"prometheus\\\"}`)\\n  - `MatrixSelector` - Range vector with time duration (e.g., `http_requests_total[5m]`)\\n  - `BinaryExpr` - Binary operations with left/right operands and optional vector matching\\n  - `AggregateExpr` - Aggregation functions (sum, avg, count, etc.) with grouping\\n  - `Call` - Function calls to built-in functions\\n  - `UnaryExpr` - Unary operations (negation)\\n  - `NumberLiteral` - Scalar numbers\\n  - `StringLiteral` - String values\\n  - `ParenExpr` - Parenthesized expressions\\n  - `SubqueryExpr` - Subqueries with time ranges\\n  - `StepInvariantExpr` - Internal optimization wrapper\\n  - `DurationExpr` - Duration literals and expressions\\n\\n### 4. Value Type System (promql/parser/value.go)\\nDefines the type system for expression validation:\\n- `ValueType` string constants: `ValueTypeVector`, `ValueTypeScalar`, `ValueTypeMatrix`, `ValueTypeString`, `ValueTypeNone`\\n- `Value` interface for runtime values with type information\\n- All Expr types implement `Type()` method returning their result type\\n\\n### 5. Function Registry (promql/parser/functions.go)\\nDefines all supported PromQL functions:\\n- `Function` struct with: Name, ArgTypes, Variadic count, ReturnType, Experimental flag\\n- `Functions` map providing a registry of 100+ built-in functions (abs, rate, increase, histogram_quantile, etc.)\\n- Functions specify their argument types for validation during type checking\\n\\n### 6. Feature Registry (promql/parser/features.go)\\n- `RegisterFeatures()` method registers available PromQL features\\n- Tracks enabled operators, aggregators, and functions\\n- Supports experimental features controlled by parser options\\n\\n### 8. Position Tracking (promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go)\\n- `PositionRange` struct tracks start/end positions in the input string\\n- Used for precise error reporting and highlighting\\n\\n## Query Execution Engine\\n\\n### 10. Engine Integration (promql/engine.go)\\nThe `Engine` struct integrates the parser into the query execution pipeline:\\n- Uses the Parser to parse query strings into AST\\n- Implements `NewInstantQuery()` and `NewRangeQuery()` to create executable queries\\n- Executes compiled query plans against TSDB data\\n- Handles timeout, cancellation, and resource management\\n- Contains EngineOpts for configuration including the parser instance\\n\\n### 11. Function Implementations (promql/functions.go)\\n- Defines `FunctionCall` type for function implementations\\n- Implements 100+ built-in functions matching the registry\\n- Functions operate on Vector, Matrix, Scalar values\\n- Examples: rate, increase, histogram_quantile, vector arithmetic, aggregation functions\\n\\n## Pipeline Flow\\n\\n1. **Input**: User provides PromQL query string\\n2. **Tokenization**: Lexer converts string to token stream\\n3. **Parsing**: YACC parser builds AST from tokens\\n4. **Validation**: `checkAST()` validates types and semantics\\n5. **Compilation**: Engine optimizes and prepares execution plan\\n6. **Execution**: Engine evaluates the query against time series data\\n7. **Output**: Returns query results (Vector, Matrix, Scalar, or String)\\n\\nAll files work together to provide a complete, type-safe PromQL query processing system with comprehensive error reporting and validation.\"\n}\n",
